| **Titles**                            | COO, CFO, VP Operations, SVP Operations, VP Client Services,  |
|                                       | SVP Client Services, VP of Business Operations, EVP           |
|                                       | Operations, VP Client Solutions, VP Finance, Regional VP      |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------------------------------+
| **Role in deal**                      | COO = Champion who drives evaluation and owns operational     |
|                                       | outcome. CFO = Margin holder who validates the business case  |
|                                       | and approves spend.                                           |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------------------------------+

**What they care about:**

- **Service quality:** Hitting client SLAs and conversion targets.
- **Protecting EBITDA:** High margin pressure from labour costs, and scaling revenue is dependent on scaling headcount.
- **Staffing correctly:** Overstaffing kills margin, understaffing kills SLAs; constant challenge given high annual attrition (20–30%+ is typical in the industry).
- **Forecast accuracy:** Aligning workforce planning with unpredictable call / outbound volumes.
- **Avoiding operational disruption:** Ensuring any new innovation must not jeopardise existing SLAs or client relationships.

**Their success metrics:** EBITDA margin (by site, by client, by program), conversion rate (outbound), resolution rate, revenue per seat per year, daily volume capacity and utilisation rate, SLA adherence and client contract renewal rate.

**Core message to them:**

> AI autopilot gives you capacity that doesn't churn, doesn't need ramping and meets SLAs. We deploy fully autonomous agents for outbound and inbound that run 24/7 in multiple languages alongside your existing team. You keep staffing lean, protect your margin and scale on demand without the hiring gamble. Your costs flex with your client's demand.

**Key proof points:** Megacable (10K+ daily outbound, 99% tagging accuracy); Viraal collections (tone-adapted by DPD stage, 25% responder rate); Digital Bank Singapore (76% promise-to-pay, regulated environment); Airline Saudi Arabia (85%+ booking success, 40% labour cost reduction).

## Persona 3: Technology Leader

+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------------------------------+
|                                       |                                                               |
+=======================================+===============================================================+
| **Titles**                            | CTO, CIO, VP Technology, VP Engineering, VP Software          |
|                                       | Engineering, CISO, VP IT, VP Digital Innovation               |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------------------------------+
| **Role in deal**                      | Technical gatekeeper. Blocks or approves based on             |
|                                       | feasibility, security, and integration.                       |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------------------------------+

**What they care about:**

- **Security, data privacy, and compliance:** One breach and the company is done. PCI-DSS, HIPAA (depending on clients), state-level regulations.
- **System reliability and uptime:** If the phones go down, nothing else matters. This is the baseline expectation.
- **Integration with existing stack:** They're running Genesys, Amazon Connect, Zendesk, or similar. Anything new must work with what they have.
- **Total cost of ownership:** Limited budget, small team, but expected to deliver innovation. They can't build like Teleperformance.

**Their success metrics:** Integration time and deployment speed, uptime and system reliability, security incidents (zero tolerance).

**Core message to them:**

> Our platform is enterprise-ready — used by the largest contact centres including Teleperformance. Deploy on cloud, on-prem, or hybrid. Enterprise-grade uptime with built-in compliance controls, content guardrails, and full audit trails. Deployments are API-first — integrates via SIP for telephony and API for CRM (Cisco and custom platforms). Secure by design, minimal internal engineering lift.

**Key proof points:** HSBC Copilot POC (98.6% factualness vs 67.5% competitor, head-to-head benchmark); S-Telco Saudi Arabia (Cisco integration, local cloud deployment, multi-language); Digital Bank Singapore (12-month production stability, continuous expansion).

## 1. Outreach Sequence

| Touch | Channel | Timing | Goal |
|-------|---------|--------|------|
| **1** | LinkedIn connection request | Day 1 | Get connected. No pitch. Be human. |
| **2** | LinkedIn message | Day 2–3 (after accept) | Build rapport. Plant event seed. Offer value. |
| **3** | Email | Day 5–7 | Persona-specific value prop. Ask for a call. |
| **4** | Email nudge | Day 12–14 | Proof point + lighter ask. |
| **5** | LinkedIn engage | Ongoing | Like / comment on their posts. Stay visible. |

---

## 2. Touch 1 — LinkedIn Connection Request

**Goal:** Get accepted. No pitch. No product.

**Character limit:** 300 characters.

**If they might attend Enterprise Connect:**

> Hi [First Name] — heading to Enterprise Connect in Vegas next month. Great to meet fellow contact center leaders. Would love to connect!

**If they're in the Southeast / CBAND Atlanta:**

> Hi [First Name] — I'll be at the CCNG event in Atlanta on Feb 26. Would love to connect if you're in the area!

**Fallback (no event):**

> Hi [First Name] — I spend my days working with BPO leaders on AI strategy for outbound ops. Would love to connect and compare notes.

---

## 3. Touch 2 — LinkedIn Message (after they accept)

**Goal:** Build rapport. Reference something personal. Plant the event seed.

**Length:** 3–5 sentences. Conversational.

> Thanks for connecting, [First Name]!
>
> [ICEBREAKER — 1–2 sentences. Reference something from their profile or company. Be specific and genuine.]
>
> I've been spending a lot of time with mid-market BPO leaders exploring how AI voice agents are transforming outbound operations. Fascinating space right now.
>
> [EVENT HOOK — choose one:]
>
> - Are you planning to be at Enterprise Connect next month? Would be great to meet in person.
> - I'll be at the CCNG event in Atlanta on the 26th — would love to grab coffee if you're nearby.
> - Would love to share some of what I'm learning if you're ever up for a quick call.

**Example (Operations Leader, Southeast):**

> Thanks for connecting, Mike!
>
> I noticed you've been at ACC Premier for over a decade — that kind of tenure in this industry says a lot. Impressive.
>
> I've been working with contact center ops leaders on something I think you'd find interesting — AI voice agents that handle outbound campaigns at scale. Seeing some really compelling results.
>
> I'll be at the CCNG event in Atlanta on Feb 26 — any chance you're in the area? Would love to compare notes.

## 6. Delivery-Model Swap-in Lines

Check the account's delivery footprint (website or master list). Swap the right hook into the Ops/Finance email where it says [SWAP IN DELIVERY-MODEL LINE].

### Onshore-Heavy (US-based delivery)

*Their reality:* Thin margins (5–8% EBITDA). Expensive US labour. Every staffing mistake hurts.

**For Finance Leader:**

> "US onshore margins at 5–8% EBITDA don't leave room for error. AI autopilot transforms the unit economics of your onshore programmes."

**For Operations Leader:**

> "Scaling onshore means opening new sites, hiring at US wages, and hoping attrition doesn't kill your ramp. AI autopilot eliminates that constraint."

### Offshore-Heavy (Philippines, India, South Africa)

*Their reality:* Healthy margins from labour arbitrage. But clients are demanding AI. The threat isn't broken margins — it's obsolescence.

**For Finance Leader:**

> "Labour arbitrage got you to 40% EBITDA. AI autopilot is the next lever — it scales volume without headcount and gives clients the AI capability they're starting to demand."

**For Operations Leader:**

> "Your offshore team handles the complex, relationship-driven work. AI autopilot takes the high-volume, scripted campaigns off their plate entirely."

### Mixed Delivery (Onshore + Offshore)

*Their reality:* Sophisticated operators already optimising which work goes where. AI is another delivery layer.

**Any persona:**

> "You already optimise work across onshore and offshore. AI autopilot is the third tier — zero labour cost, infinite scale, per-outcome pricing. Route your most repetitive workflows there."

---

## 7. Objection Handling

| Objection | Response |
|-----------|----------|
| "We're already doing AI" | "That's great — most BPOs we talk to have started with internal tools or copilots. Where we see the biggest gap is in outbound production. Are you running AI agents on live outbound campaigns today?" |
| "We're not ready for AI" | "That's actually the best time to start a pilot. A focused outbound deployment gives you real data to build your AI strategy around — not theory." |
| "Send me some information" | "Of course. But the most valuable thing I can share is what we're learning from deployments with operators like yours. Can we do 15 minutes so I can tailor what I send?" |
| "We tried AI and it didn't work" | "That's more common than you'd think. Most pilots fail because of execution, not technology. Our approach is operationally led — we design the scripts and workflows, not just plug in tech. What did you try before?" |
| "We can build this ourselves" | "We see a lot of that. Teams usually get to 60–80% quality. The last 20% — uptime, compliance, multi-language, continuous optimisation — is where it breaks in production. Happy to show you where the gap typically is." |
| "What's it cost?" | "It depends on the use case and volume. We offer outcome-aligned pricing — per call, per outcome, or revenue sharing. The point is you don't pay unless it works." |
| "I need to talk to my team" | "Absolutely. Would it help if I put together a brief with the relevant case studies so you have something concrete to share? Who else would typically be involved in evaluating something like this?" |
| "Our clients won't accept AI" | "Our agents are human-like and multilingual. In production, clients often can't tell the difference. Start with use cases where AI is clearly additive — booking confirmations, payment reminders, lead qualification." |

---

## 8. Do's and Don'ts

**Do:**

- Lead with **AI autopilot** — own this term
- Mention **both outbound and inbound**, emphasise outbound
- Talk **margin and EBITDA** directly with COO/CFO
- Reference **Teleperformance** early for credibility
- Use **events as conversation starters**
- **Personalise every message** — use icebreaker insight from contact list
- Position Calanthia as a **senior industry expert**, not a salesperson
- Keep LinkedIn messages **short and conversational**
- Keep first-touch emails **under 150 words**

**Don't:**

- Don't say "copilot" or "agent assist" — we do **full autopilot**
- Don't lead with product features or a demo offer
- Don't send the same message to all three personas
- Don't use "early access" framing (PH positioning, doesn't work for US)
- Don't position as a startup
- Don't batch-send identical emails for Cohort 1 — personalise each one
- Don't use "APO Labs" — we are **Dyna.ai** in the US market

---

| Event | Date | Location | Use For |
|-------|------|----------|---------|
| **CCNG / CBAND Atlanta** | Feb 26, 2026 | Atlanta, GA | Southeast contacts. Calanthia attending. |
| **Enterprise Connect** | Mar 10–12, 2026 | Las Vegas, NV | All US contacts. Major vendor-neutral event. |
| **ICMI Digital Experience** | Apr 8, 2026 | Virtual (free) | Lighter hook. "Tuning into ICMI next month?" |
| **Frost & Sullivan MindXchange** | Apr 12–15, 2026 | Fort Lauderdale, FL | Senior execs. Invite-style format. |
| **Customer Contact Week (CCW)** | Jun 22–25, 2026 | Las Vegas, NV | Biggest CC event. Use after initial contact. |

**If they're going:** "Looking forward to seeing you there. Let's find 20 minutes to meet."

**If they're NOT going:** "I don't blame you — Vegas in March is a lot. Would you be up for a call instead? I can share my takeaways from the event afterwards."

**If no response to event hook:** Drop it. Move to email with persona-specific value prop.

## 6. Objection Handling

+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+
| **Objection**                         | **Response**                          |
+=======================================+=======================================+
| "We're already doing AI"              | "That's great — where we see the      |
|                                       | biggest gap is in outbound            |
|                                       | production. Are you running AI        |
|                                       | agents on live outbound campaigns     |
|                                       | today?"                               |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+
| "We're not ready for AI"              | "That's actually the best time to     |
|                                       | start a pilot. A focused outbound     |
|                                       | deployment gives you real data to     |
|                                       | build your AI strategy around."       |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+
| "Send me some information"            | "Of course. But the most valuable     |
|                                       | thing I can share is what we're       |
|                                       | learning from operators like you.     |
|                                       | Can we do 15 minutes so I can         |
|                                       | tailor what I send?"                  |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+
| "We tried AI and it didn't work"      | "Most pilots fail because of          |
|                                       | execution, not technology. Our        |
|                                       | approach is operationally led — we    |
|                                       | design the scripts and workflows.     |
|                                       | What did you try before?"             |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+
| "We can build this ourselves"         | "Teams usually get to 60–80%. The     |
|                                       | last 20% — uptime, compliance,        |
|                                       | multi-language, continuous            |
|                                       | optimisation — is where it breaks.    |
|                                       | Happy to show you where the gap is."  |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+
| "What's it cost?"                     | "Outcome-aligned pricing — per call,  |
|                                       | per outcome, or revenue sharing.      |
|                                       | You don't pay unless it works."       |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+
| "Our clients won't accept AI"         | "Our agents are human-like and        |
|                                       | multilingual. Start with additive     |
|                                       | use cases — booking confirmations,    |
|                                       | payment reminders, lead               |
|                                       | qualification."                       |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+
| "I need to talk to my team"           | "Would it help if I put together a    |
|                                       | brief with the relevant case studies  |
|                                       | so you have something concrete to     |
|                                       | share? Who else would be involved?"   |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+

## 7. Do's and Don'ts

+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+
| **Do**                                | **Don't**                             |
+=======================================+=======================================+
| Lead with **AI autopilot**            | Don't say "copilot" or "agent         |
|                                       | assist" — we do full autopilot        |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+
| Mention both outbound and inbound,    | Don't lead with product features      |
| emphasise outbound                    | or a demo offer                       |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+
| Talk margin and EBITDA directly       | Don't send the same message to        |
| with COO/CFO                          | all three personas                    |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+
| Reference Teleperformance early       | Don't use "early access" framing      |
| for credibility                       | (PH positioning, not for US)          |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+
| Use events as conversation starters   | Don't position as a startup           |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+
| Personalise every message             | Don't batch-send identical emails     |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+
| Position Calanthia as a senior        | Don't use "APO Labs" — we are         |
| industry expert, not a salesperson    | **Dyna.ai** in the US market          |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+
| Keep first-touch emails under         | Don't shy away from talking about     |
| 150 words                             | replacing manual volume — C-suite     |
|                                       | cares about margin, not headcount     |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+

Good questions. Here's my recommendation:

**Where to put them: the Messaging Playbook, not the Persona Map.**

The Persona Map is the approval doc — clean, short, stays as-is. The case studies are operational: Calanthia grabs the right one when she's writing a specific message to a specific person. That's playbook territory. I'd add a case study quick-reference table as a new section.

**How to handle the vertical-specificity:**

This is actually your strength, not a problem. BPOs serve specific client industries — and when Calanthia reaches out to a BPO, she can check what industries that BPO serves (from their website or the master list) and pick the matching case study. The framing should be around the **use case** (outbound telesales, collections, booking confirmations, renewals), not the end-client's industry. The BPO doesn't care that IZZI is a telco — they care that Dyna can do outbound telesales upsell at 10K+ daily volume with 4.7% conversion.

So the table should be organised by **use case**, with the client industry as a secondary tag. That way Calanthia can think: "This BPO does collections for banks → grab the Viraal or Digital Bank case study."

**On naming restrictions — from the doc:**

- **Toyota and Teleperformance:** Can use name AND logo in writing
- **HSBC and Chubb:** Verbal mention ONLY — don't put in emails or LinkedIn messages
- **Others** (IZZI, Megacable, Sands Macau, Lifenet, Viraal, MenuSifu, Digital Bank Singapore, Airline Saudi): Permissions not stated in this doc. Until confirmed, safest to reference generically in written outreach ("a major Mexican telco", "a digital bank in Singapore", "a leading Japanese insurer") and only name-drop verbally on calls.

**What I'd build:**

A case study reference table in the playbook with columns:

| Use Case | Industry | Named/Anonymous | Key Metrics | Best For Persona | When to Use |
|----------|----------|-----------------|-------------|------------------|-------------|

This gives Calanthia a quick lookup: "I'm writing to a COO at a BPO that does collections for banks → grab the Digital Bank Singapore row → use the metrics from that row in my email."

That specificity is what makes personalization feel real rather than templated, and it should drive everything else.

**Your connection request:**
> Hey [first name], I spend my days working with BPO leaders on their AI strategy. Great to connect

- "I spend my days working with BPO leaders" — positions you well, but it's self-focused. The recipient is thinking "why should I accept?" not "what does this person do?"
- "Great to connect" — premature. You haven't connected yet. Small thing but it reads like a template.

- This reads like a brochure. It lists every pain point hoping one sticks, which is the tell of a template. The "/" construction is the giveaway — Calanthia has to pick one, and if she picks wrong it feels generic.
- "thought you may be interested in hearing about what your peers are doing to evolve" — "what your peers are doing" is a classic sales trigger. It works on calls, but in writing it can feel manipulative.

**The core principle:** Every sentence should either be about *them* or offer *something genuinely useful*. If it's about you or your service, cut it.

Let me rewrite these and build a proper decision tree. I'll update the playbook.

  new_string: ## 2. LinkedIn — Connection Request

**Goal:** Get accepted. That's it. No pitch, no product, no cleverness. 300 character limit.

**Rule:** Every request should feel like it could only have been sent to this one person. If it could go to 50 people unchanged, rewrite it.

### Decision tree: which connection request to send

```
Do I have something SPECIFIC about this person?
(Recent post, shared connection, something notable about their company)
│
├─ YES → Use the PERSONAL request
│
└─ NO → Is there an upcoming event they might attend?
     │
     ├─ Southeast contact → CBAND Atlanta request
     ├─ Any US contact → Enterprise Connect request
     │
     └─ No event fits → Use the INDUSTRY PEER request
```

### Option A — Personal (best, use whenever possible)

> Hi [First Name] — [one specific thing about them]. Would love to connect.

Examples:

> Hi Mike — saw your post about attrition challenges in nearshore ops. That resonated. Would love to connect.

> Hi Sarah — congratulations on the Frost & Sullivan recognition for ResultsCX. Would love to connect.

> Hi James — I noticed you've been at Qualfon for over a decade. That kind of tenure in this industry is rare. Would love to connect.

### Option B — Event (when you don't have a personal hook)

**CBAND Atlanta:**

> Hi [First Name] — I'll be at the CCNG event in Atlanta on Feb 26. Would love to connect if you're in the area.

**Enterprise Connect:**

> Hi [First Name] — heading to Enterprise Connect next month. Would love to connect with fellow contact center leaders.

### Option C — Industry peer (fallback, no personal hook, no event)

> Hi [First Name] — I work with mid-market BPO leaders on AI strategy for voice operations. Would love to connect and compare notes.

---

## 3. LinkedIn — Follow-up Message (after they accept)

**Goal:** Build rapport. Offer something genuinely useful. Create a reason to talk — don't ask for anything yet.

**Rule:** Lead with *them*, not with you. The first sentence after "thanks for connecting" should be about something *they* did, said, or care about.

### Decision tree: which follow-up to send

```
Do I have an icebreaker?
(Something specific from their profile, posts, company news)
│
├─ YES ─── Is there an upcoming event?
│           │
│           ├─ YES → ICEBREAKER + EVENT message
│           └─ NO  → ICEBREAKER + VALUE OFFER message
│
└─ NO ──── Is there an upcoming event?
            │
            ├─ YES → COMPANY COMPLIMENT + EVENT message
            └─ NO  → COMPANY COMPLIMENT + VALUE OFFER message
```

### Template A — Icebreaker + Event (strongest)

> Thanks for connecting, [First Name].
>
> [ICEBREAKER — 1–2 sentences. Be specific. Reference a post, a milestone, something you noticed about their company. NOT a generic compliment.]
>
> I'll be at [EVENT] — are you planning to go? I've been spending time with BPO leaders exploring how AI is changing outbound operations and would love to compare notes in person.

**Example:**

> Thanks for connecting, Mike.
>
> I saw you've been at ACC Premier for over a decade — that kind of tenure in this industry says a lot about the culture you've built there.
>
> I'll be at the CCNG event in Atlanta on Feb 26 — any chance you're going? I've been talking to a lot of mid-market BPO leaders about what's actually working with AI in outbound, and I think you'd find the conversations interesting.

### Template B — Icebreaker + Value offer (no event)

> Thanks for connecting, [First Name].
>
> [ICEBREAKER — 1–2 sentences.]
>
> I've been having some really interesting conversations with BPO leaders about what's actually working with AI in voice operations — not the hype, the real results. Would be curious to hear how [Company] is thinking about it. Happy to share what I'm learning if that's useful.

### Template C — Company compliment + Event (no personal icebreaker)

> Thanks for connecting, [First Name].
>
> [Company] has a strong reputation in [their specialty — collections, customer service, etc.]. Impressive what you've built.
>
> I'll be at [EVENT] — are you planning to go? Would love to meet in person.

### Template D — Company compliment + Value offer (no icebreaker, no event)

> Thanks for connecting, [First Name].
>
> [Company] has a strong reputation in [their specialty]. I've been having some interesting conversations with BPO leaders about what's actually delivering results with AI in voice operations. Would be curious to hear how you're thinking about it — happy to share what I'm seeing if that's useful.

### What makes a GOOD icebreaker vs a BAD one

+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+
| **Good (specific, shows you looked)** | **Bad (generic, could be anyone)**    |
+=======================================+=======================================+
| "Saw your post about the challenge    | "I see you're in the BPO space"       |
| of scaling nearshore — that           |                                       |
| resonated"                            |                                       |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+
| "Congratulations on 10 years at       | "Your company has a great             |
| [Company] — that tenure says a lot"   | reputation"                           |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+
| "I noticed [Company] just expanded    | "I know you're championing your       |
| into the Philippines — exciting       | company's strategy"                   |
| move"                                 |                                       |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+
| "Your comment on [Person]'s post      | "I spend my days with BPO leaders     |
| about AI in CX was spot on"           | who are looking to stay competitive"  |
+---------------------------------------+---------------------------------------+

[Tool call] Write
  path: /Users/alicewyatt/repos/agent-playground/scripts/generate-outreach.ts
  contents: /**
 * Generate personalised Touch 1/2/3 messaging for each prospect in Cohort 1.
 * Uses the messaging playbook templates + prospect data.
 * Output: data/personalised-outreach.md
 */
import { config } from "dotenv";
import { generateText } from "ai";
import { anthropic } from "@ai-sdk/anthropic";
import fs from "fs";
import path from "path";
import { fileURLToPath } from "url";
import { parse } from "csv-parse/sync";

config();

const __dirname = path.dirname(fileURLToPath(import.meta.url));

interface Prospect {
  fullName: string;
  firstName: string;
  lastName: string;
  jobTitle: string;
  company: string;
  location: string;
  persona: string;
  eventHook: string;
  isSoutheast: boolean;
  activeLinkedIn: boolean;
  icebreaker: string;
  summaryOfRole: string;
  linkedinProfile: string;
  email: string;
  companyTenure: string;
  notableExperience: string;
  firstDegree: string;
  calanthiaFirstDegree: string;
}

function assignPersona(title: string): string {
  const t = title.toLowerCase();
  if (
    t.includes("ceo") || t.includes("chief executive") || t.includes("president") ||
    t.includes("founder") || t.includes("owner") || t.includes("chairman") ||
    t.includes("managing partner")
  ) return "Executive Sponsor";
  if (
    t.includes("cto") || t.includes("chief technology") || t.includes("chief information") ||
    t.includes("cio") || t.includes("ciso") || t.includes("vp technology") ||
    t.includes("vp engineering") || t.includes("vp software") || t.includes("vp it") ||
    t.includes("vp digital innovation") || t.includes("vp, technology") ||
    t.includes("vice president of technology") || t.includes("vice president, technology") ||
    t.includes("call center technologies") || t.includes("senior vice president of technology")
  ) return "Technology Leader";
  return "Operations & Finance Leader";
}

function assignEventHook(location: string): string {
  const loc = location.toLowerCase();
  const seStates = [
    "georgia", "atlanta", "florida", "north carolina", "south carolina",
    "tennessee", "alabama", "mississippi", "virginia", "louisiana"
  ];
  if (seStates.some(s => loc.includes(s))) return "CBAND Atlanta (Feb 26)";
  return "Enterprise Connect (Mar 10-12, Las Vegas)";
}

function isSoutheastLocation(location: string): boolean {
  const loc = location.toLowerCase();
  const seStates = [
    "georgia", "atlanta", "florida", "north carolina", "south carolina",
    "tennessee", "alabama", "mississippi", "virginia", "louisiana"
  ];
  return seStates.some(s => loc.includes(s));
}

async function generateMessaging(prospect: Prospect): Promise<string> {
  const hasIcebreaker = prospect.icebreaker.trim().length > 10;
  const hasEvent = prospect.eventHook.length > 0;
  const eventName = prospect.eventHook.includes("CBAND") ? "CCNG event in Atlanta on Feb 26" : "Enterprise Connect in Las Vegas next month";

  const connectionContext = prospect.firstDegree || prospect.calanthiaFirstDegree
    ? `\nConnection: ${prospect.firstDegree ? "Alice is a 1st degree connection" : ""}${prospect.calanthiaFirstDegree ? "Calanthia is a 1st degree connection" : ""}`
    : "";

  const prompt = `You are writing LinkedIn and email outreach for Calanthia Mei, an AI entrepreneur and Strategic Advisor at Dyna.ai, reaching out to US mid-market BPO leaders.

PROSPECT:
- Name: ${prospect.fullName} (first name: ${prospect.firstName})
- Title: ${prospect.jobTitle}
- Company: ${prospect.company}
- Location: ${prospect.location}
- Persona: ${prospect.persona}
- Event hook: ${prospect.eventHook}${connectionContext}
${prospect.companyTenure ? `- Tenure: ${prospect.companyTenure}` : ""}
${prospect.notableExperience ? `- Notable experience: ${prospect.notableExperience}` : ""}
${hasIcebreaker ? `- Icebreaker insight: ${prospect.icebreaker}` : "- No icebreaker insight available."}
${prospect.summaryOfRole ? `- Role summary: ${prospect.summaryOfRole}` : ""}

RULES:
- Tone: peer-to-peer, senior executive to senior executive. Calanthia is NOT selling. She's genuinely curious and offering value.
- Never mention Dyna.ai or any product in Touch 1 or Touch 2.
- Never pitch in Touch 1 or Touch 2. Touch 3 (email) is where the value prop goes.
- Be specific — no generic compliments. If you don't have something specific, reference the company's reputation or specialty instead.
- Keep Touch 1 under 300 characters including the name.
- Keep Touch 2 to 3-5 sentences. Conversational.
- Keep Touch 3 (email) under 150 words for the body.
- For Touch 3, match the persona:
  - Executive Sponsor: lead with competitive pressure, AI autopilot, scale without headcount
  - Operations & Finance Leader: lead with elastic capacity, no churn, margin protection, proof points (10K daily calls, 99% accuracy, 76% promise-to-pay, 40% cost reduction)
  - Technology Leader: lead with the 60-80% problem, production-grade platform, deployment flexibility, integration

Write exactly three pieces:

TOUCH 1 — LINKEDIN CONNECTION REQUEST (under 300 chars):
${hasIcebreaker ? "Use a personal hook from the icebreaker insight." : hasEvent ? `Use the event hook: ${eventName}.` : "Use an industry peer approach."}

TOUCH 2 — LINKEDIN FOLLOW-UP MESSAGE (after they accept, 3-5 sentences):
${hasIcebreaker && hasEvent ? "Use icebreaker + event approach." : hasIcebreaker ? "Use icebreaker + value offer approach." : hasEvent ? "Use company compliment + event approach." : "Use company compliment + value offer approach."}
End with either an event ask ("are you going?") or a soft value offer ("happy to share what I'm learning").

TOUCH 3 — EMAIL (persona: ${prospect.persona}):
Include a subject line, then the email body. Reference the LinkedIn connection. Use the persona-appropriate value prop and proof points. End with a call to action asking for a 20-minute call.

Format your response EXACTLY like this (no other text):

**Touch 1 — Connection Request**
[the message]

**Touch 2 — LinkedIn Message**
[the message]

**Touch 3 — Email**
Subject: [subject line]

[email body including "Best, Calanthia" sign-off]`;

  const result = await generateText({
    model: anthropic("claude-sonnet-4-20250514"),
    prompt,
    maxTokens: 800,
    temperature: 0.7,
  });

  return result.text;
}

async function main() {
  const csvPath = path.join(__dirname, "..", "Downloads", "Top Contacts 2026 - Top Contacts.csv");
  const altPath = "/Users/alicewyatt/Downloads/Top Contacts 2026 - Top Contacts.csv";
  const filePath = fs.existsSync(csvPath) ? csvPath : altPath;

  const raw = fs.readFileSync(filePath, "utf-8");
  const records = parse(raw, { columns: true, skip_empty_lines: true });

  const prospects: Prospect[] = records
    .filter((r: Record<string, string>) => {
      const name = (r["Full Name"] || "").trim();
      if (!name) return false;
      const active = r["Active on LinkedIn (last 90 days)"] === "1" || r["Active on LinkedIn (last 90 days)"] === "True";
      const se = isSoutheastLocation(r["Location"] || "");
      return active || se;
    })
    .map((r: Record<string, string>) => {
      const fullName = r["Full Name"].trim();
      const firstName = r["First Name"]?.trim() || fullName.split(" ")[0];
      const lastName = r["Last Name"]?.trim() || "";
      return {
        fullName,
        firstName,
        lastName,
        jobTitle: r["Job Title"] || "",
        company: r["Company Name"] || "",
        location: r["Location"] || "",
        persona: assignPersona(r["Job Title"] || ""),
        eventHook: assignEventHook(r["Location"] || ""),
        isSoutheast: isSoutheastLocation(r["Location"] || ""),
        activeLinkedIn: r["Active on LinkedIn (last 90 days)"] === "1" || r["Active on LinkedIn (last 90 days)"] === "True",
        icebreaker: r["Icebreaker Insight"] || "",
        summaryOfRole: r["Summary of Role"] || "",
        linkedinProfile: r["LinkedIn Profile"] || "",
        email: r["Contact Email"] || "",
        companyTenure: r["Company Tenure"] || "",
        notableExperience: r["Notable Previous Experience"] || "",
        firstDegree: r["First Degree Connection [Alice or Calanthia]"] || "",
        calanthiaFirstDegree: r["Calanthia First Degree"] || "",
      };
    });

  console.log(`Found ${prospects.length} prospects (active LinkedIn or Southeast)`);

  const lines: string[] = [
    "# Personalised Outreach — Cohort 1",
    "",
    `> Generated: ${new Date().toLocaleDateString("en-GB", { day: "numeric", month: "long", year: "numeric" })}`,
    `> Total prospects: ${prospects.length}`,
    "",
    "---",
    "",
  ];

  for (let i = 0; i < prospects.length; i++) {
    const p = prospects[i];
    console.log(`[${i + 1}/${prospects.length}] ${p.fullName} — ${p.jobTitle} at ${p.company}`);

    try {
      const messaging = await generateMessaging(p);

      lines.push(`## ${i + 1}. ${p.fullName}`);
      lines.push("");
      lines.push(`| | |`);
      lines.push(`|---|---|`);
      lines.push(`| **Title** | ${p.jobTitle} |`);
      lines.push(`| **Company** | ${p.company} |`);
      lines.push(`| **Persona** | ${p.persona} |`);
      lines.push(`| **Location** | ${p.location} |`);
      lines.push(`| **Event hook** | ${p.eventHook} |`);
      lines.push(`| **LinkedIn** | ${p.linkedinProfile} |`);
      lines.push(`| **Email** | ${p.email} |`);
      lines.push("");
      lines.push(messaging);
      lines.push("");
      lines.push("---");
      lines.push("");
    } catch (err) {
      console.error(`  ERROR for ${p.fullName}:`, err);
      lines.push(`## ${i + 1}. ${p.fullName}`);
      lines.push("");
      lines.push(`**Error generating messaging — do manually.**`);
      lines.push("");
      lines.push("---");
      lines.push("");
    }
  }

  const outPath = path.join(__dirname, "..", "data", "personalised-outreach.md");
  fs.writeFileSync(outPath, lines.join("\n"), "utf-8");
  console.log(`\nDone! Wrote ${outPath}`);
}

main().catch(console.error);

  new_string: function assignPersona(title: string): string {
  const t = title.toLowerCase();

  // Executive Sponsor — top-level titles. Check CEO/Founder first.
  const isExec = t.includes("ceo") || t.includes("chief executive") ||
    t.includes("founder") || t.includes("owner") || t.includes("chairman") ||
    t.includes("managing partner");
  // "President" counts as exec ONLY if not "Vice President"
  const isPresident = t.includes("president") && !t.includes("vice president");
  if (isExec || isPresident) return "Executive Sponsor";

  // Technology Leader
  if (
    t.includes("cto") || t.includes("chief technology") || t.includes("chief information") ||
    t.includes("cio") || t.includes("ciso") ||
    /\bvp\b.*technolog/i.test(title) || t.includes("vp engineering") ||
    t.includes("vp software") || t.includes("vp it") || t.includes("vp digital innovation") ||
    t.includes("vice president of technology") || t.includes("vice president, technology") ||
    t.includes("call center technologies") || t.includes("senior vice president of technology") ||
    t.includes("cybersecurity") || t.includes("innovation")
  ) return "Technology Leader";

  // Everything else: Operations & Finance Leader
  return "Operations & Finance Leader";
}
